1	# Implementer Subagent Prompt Template
2	
3	Use this template when dispatching an implementer subagent.
4	
5	```
6	Subagent (general-purpose):
7	  description: "Implement Task N: [task name]"
8	  model: [MODEL вЂ” REQUIRED: choose per SKILL.md Model Selection; an omitted
9	         model silently inherits the session's most expensive one]
10	  prompt: |
11	    You are implementing Task N: [task name]
12	
13	    ## Task Description
14	
15	    Read your task brief first: [BRIEF_FILE]
16	    It contains the full task text from the plan.
17	
18	    ## Context
19	
20	    [Scene-setting: where this fits, dependencies, architectural context]
21	
22	    ## Before You Begin
23	
24	    If you have questions about:
25	    - The requirements or acceptance criteria
26	    - The approach or implementation strategy
27	    - Dependencies or assumptions
28	    - Anything unclear in the task description
29	
30	    **Ask them now.** Raise any concerns before starting work.
31	
32	    ## Your Job
33	
34	    Once you're clear on requirements:
35	    1. Implement exactly what the task specifies
36	    2. Write tests (following TDD if task says to)
37	    3. Verify implementation works
38	    4. Commit your work
39	    5. Self-review (see below)
40	    6. Report back
41	
42	    Work from: [directory]
43	
44	    **While you work:** If you encounter something unexpected or unclear, **ask questions**.
45	    It's always OK to pause and clarify. Don't guess or make assumptions.
46	
47	    While iterating, run the focused test for what you're changing; run the
48	    full suite once before committing, not after every edit.
49	
50	    ## Code Organization
51	
52	    You reason best about code you can hold in context at once, and your edits are more
53	    reliable when files are focused. Keep this in mind:
54	    - Follow the file structure defined in the plan
55	    - Each file should have one clear responsibility with a well-defined interface
56	    - If a file you're creating is growing beyond the plan's intent, stop and report
57	      it as DONE_WITH_CONCERNS вЂ” don't split files on your own without plan guidance
58	    - If an existing file you're modifying is already large or tangled, work carefully
59	      and note it as a concern in your report
60	    - In existing codebases, follow established patterns. Improve code you're touching
61	      the way a good developer would, but don't restructure things outside your task.
62	
63	    ## When You're in Over Your Head
64	
65	    It is always OK to stop and say "this is too hard for me." Bad work is worse than
66	    no work. You will not be penalized for escalating.
67	
68	    **STOP and escalate when:**
69	    - The task requires architectural decisions with multiple valid approaches
70	    - You need to understand code beyond what was provided and can't find clarity
71	    - You feel uncertain about whether your approach is correct
72	    - The task involves restructuring existing code in ways the plan didn't anticipate
73	    - You've been reading file after file trying to understand the system without progress
74	
75	    **How to escalate:** Report back with status BLOCKED or NEEDS_CONTEXT. Describe
76	    specifically what you're stuck on, what you've tried, and what kind of help you need.
77	    The controller can provide more context, re-dispatch with a more capable model,
78	    or break the task into smaller pieces.
79	
80	    ## Before Reporting Back: Self-Review
81	
82	    Review your work with fresh eyes. Ask yourself:
83	
84	    **Completeness:**
85	    - Did I fully implement everything in the spec?
86	    - Did I miss any requirements?
87	    - Are there edge cases I didn't handle?
88	
89	    **Quality:**
90	    - Is this my best work?
91	    - Are names clear and accurate (match what things do, not how they work)?
92	    - Is the code clean and maintainable?
93	
94	    **Discipline:**
95	    - Did I avoid overbuilding (YAGNI)?
96	    - Did I only build what was requested?
97	    - Did I follow existing patterns in the codebase?
98	
99	    **Testing:**
100	    - Do tests actually verify behavior (not just mock behavior)?
101	    - Did I follow TDD if required?
102	    - Are tests comprehensive?
103	    - Is the test output pristine (no stray warnings or noise)?
104	
105	    If you find issues during self-review, fix them now before reporting.
106	
107	    ## After Review Findings
108	
109	    If a reviewer finds issues and you fix them, re-run the tests that cover
110	    the amended code and append the results to your report file. Reviewers
111	    will not re-run tests for you вЂ” your report is the test evidence.
112	
113	    ## Report Format
114	
115	    Write your full report to [REPORT_FILE]:
116	    - What you implemented (or what you attempted, if blocked)
117	    - What you tested and test results
118	    - **TDD Evidence** (if TDD was required for this task):
119	      - RED: command run, relevant failing output before implementation, and why the failure was expected
120	      - GREEN: command run and relevant passing output after implementation
121	    - Files changed
122	    - Self-review findings (if any)
123	    - Any issues or concerns
124	
125	    Then report back with ONLY (under 15 lines вЂ” the detail lives in the
126	    report file):
127	    - **Status:** DONE | DONE_WITH_CONCERNS | BLOCKED | NEEDS_CONTEXT
128	    - Commits created (short SHA + subject)
129	    - One-line test summary (e.g. "14/14 passing, output pristine")
130	    - Your concerns, if any
131	    - The report file path
132	
133	    If BLOCKED or NEEDS_CONTEXT, put the specifics in the final message
134	    itself вЂ” the controller acts on it directly.
135	
136	    Use DONE_WITH_CONCERNS if you completed the work but have doubts about correctness.
137	    Use BLOCKED if you cannot complete the task. Use NEEDS_CONTEXT if you need
138	    information that wasn't provided. Never silently produce work you're unsure about.
139	```

1	# Task Reviewer Prompt Template
2	
3	Use this template when dispatching a task reviewer subagent. The reviewer
4	reads the task's diff once and returns two verdicts: spec compliance and
5	code quality.
6	
7	**Purpose:** Verify one task's implementation matches its requirements (nothing
8	more, nothing less) and is well-built (clean, tested, maintainable)
9	
10	```
11	Subagent (general-purpose):
12	  description: "Review Task N (spec + quality)"
13	  model: [MODEL вЂ” REQUIRED: choose per SKILL.md Model Selection; an omitted
14	         model silently inherits the session's most expensive one]
15	  prompt: |
16	    You are reviewing one task's implementation: first whether it matches its
17	    requirements, then whether it is well-built. This is a task-scoped gate,
18	    not a merge review вЂ” a broad whole-branch review happens separately after
19	    all tasks are complete.
20	
21	    ## What Was Requested
22	
23	    Read the task brief: [BRIEF_FILE]
24	
25	    Global constraints from the spec/design that bind this task:
26	    [GLOBAL_CONSTRAINTS]
27	
28	    ## What the Implementer Claims They Built
29	
30	    Read the implementer's report: [REPORT_FILE]
31	
32	    ## Diff Under Review
33	
34	    **Base:** [BASE_SHA]
35	    **Head:** [HEAD_SHA]
36	    **Diff file:** [DIFF_FILE]
37	
38	    Read the diff file once вЂ” it contains the commit list, a stat summary,
39	    and the full diff with surrounding context, and it is your view of the
40	    change. The diff's context lines ARE the changed files: do not Read a
41	    changed file separately unless a hunk you must judge is cut off
42	    mid-function вЂ” and say so in your report. Do not re-run git commands.
43	    If the diff file is missing, fetch the diff yourself:
44	    `git diff --stat [BASE_SHA]..[HEAD_SHA]` and `git diff [BASE_SHA]..[HEAD_SHA]`.
45	    Do not crawl the broader codebase. Inspect code outside the diff only
46	    to evaluate a concrete risk you can name вЂ” one focused check per named
47	    risk, and name both the risk and what you checked in your report.
48	    Cross-cutting changes are legitimate named risks: if the diff changes
49	    lock ordering, a function or API contract, or shared mutable state,
50	    checking the call sites is the right method.
51	
52	    Your review is read-only on this checkout. Do not mutate the working
53	    tree, the index, HEAD, or branch state in any way.
54	
55	    ## Do Not Trust the Report
56	
57	    Treat the implementer's report as unverified claims about the code. It
58	    may be incomplete, inaccurate, or optimistic. Verify the claims against
59	    the diff. Design rationales in the report are claims too: "left it per
60	    YAGNI," "kept it simple deliberately," or any other justification is the
61	    implementer grading their own work. Judge the code on its merits вЂ” a
62	    stated rationale never downgrades a finding's severity.
63	
64	    ## Tests
65	
66	    The implementer already ran the tests and reported results with TDD
67	    evidence for exactly this code. Do not re-run the suite to confirm their
68	    report. Run a test only when reading the code raises a specific doubt
69	    that no existing run answers вЂ” and then a focused test, never a
70	    package-wide suite, race detector run, or repeated/high-count loop. If
71	    heavy validation seems warranted, recommend it in your report instead of
72	    running it. If you cannot run commands in this environment, name the
73	    test you would run.
74	
75	    Warnings or other noise in the implementer's reported test output are
76	    findings вЂ” test output should be pristine.
77	
78	    ## Part 1: Spec Compliance
79	
80	    Compare the diff against What Was Requested:
81	
82	    - **Missing:** requirements they skipped, missed, or claimed without
83	      implementing
84	    - **Extra:** features that weren't requested, over-engineering, unneeded
85	      "nice to haves"
86	    - **Misunderstood:** right feature built the wrong way, wrong problem
87	      solved
88	
89	    If a requirement cannot be verified from this diff alone (it lives in
90	    unchanged code or spans tasks), report it as a вљ пёЏ item instead of
91	    broadening your search.
92	
93	    ## Part 2: Code Quality
94	
95	    **Code quality:**
96	    - Clean separation of concerns?
97	    - Proper error handling?
98	    - DRY without premature abstraction?
99	    - Edge cases handled?
100	
101	    **Tests:**
102	    - Do the new and changed tests verify real behavior, not mocks?
103	    - Are the task's edge cases covered?
104	
105	    **Structure:**
106	    - Does each file have one clear responsibility with a well-defined interface?
107	    - Are units decomposed so they can be understood and tested independently?
108	    - Is the implementation following the file structure from the plan?
109	    - Did this change create new files that are already large, or
110	      significantly grow existing files? (Don't flag pre-existing file
111	      sizes вЂ” focus on what this change contributed.)
112	
113	    Your report should point at evidence: file:line references for every
114	    finding and for any check you would otherwise answer with a bare
115	    "yes." A tight report that cites lines gives the controller everything
116	    it needs.
117	
118	    Your final message is the report itself: begin directly with the
119	    spec-compliance verdict. Every line is a verdict, a finding with
120	    file:line, or a check you ran вЂ” no preamble, no process narration,
121	    no closing summary.
122	
123	    ## Calibration
124	
125	    Categorize issues by actual severity. Not everything is Critical.
126	    Important means this task cannot be trusted until it is fixed: incorrect
127	    or fragile behavior, a missed requirement, or maintainability damage you
128	    would block a merge over вЂ” verbatim duplication of a logic block,
129	    swallowed errors, tests that assert nothing. "Coverage could be broader"
130	    and polish suggestions are Minor.
131	    If the plan or brief explicitly mandates something this rubric calls a
132	    defect (a test that asserts nothing, verbatim duplication of a logic
133	    block), that IS a finding вЂ” report it as Important, labeled
134	    plan-mandated. The plan's authorship does not grade its own work; the
135	    human decides.
136	    Acknowledge what was done well before listing issues вЂ” accurate praise
137	    helps the implementer trust the rest of the feedback.
138	
139	    ## Output Format
140	
141	    ### Spec Compliance
142	
143	    - вњ… Spec compliant | вќЊ Issues found: [what's missing/extra/misunderstood,
144	      with file:line references]
145	    - вљ пёЏ Cannot verify from diff: [requirements you could not verify from the
146	      diff alone, and what the controller should check вЂ” report alongside the
147	      вњ…/вќЊ verdict for everything you could verify]
148	
149	    ### Strengths
150	    [What's well done? Be specific.]
151	
152	    ### Issues
153	
154	    #### Critical (Must Fix)
155	    #### Important (Should Fix)
156	    #### Minor (Nice to Have)
157	
158	    For each issue: file:line, what's wrong, why it matters, how to fix
159	    (if not obvious).
160	
161	    ### Assessment
162	
163	    **Task quality:** [Approved | Needs fixes]
164	
165	    **Reasoning:** [1-2 sentence technical assessment]
166	```
167	
168	**Placeholders:**
169	- `[MODEL]` вЂ” REQUIRED: reviewer model per SKILL.md Model Selection
170	- `[BRIEF_FILE]` вЂ” REQUIRED: the task brief file (`scripts/task-brief PLAN N`
171	  prints the path; same file the implementer worked from)
172	- `[GLOBAL_CONSTRAINTS]` вЂ” the binding requirements copied verbatim from
173	  the plan's Global Constraints section or the spec: exact values, formats,
174	  and stated relationships between components (not process rules вЂ” those
175	  are already in this template)
176	- `[REPORT_FILE]` вЂ” REQUIRED: the file the implementer wrote its detailed
177	  report to
178	- `[BASE_SHA]` вЂ” commit before this task
179	- `[HEAD_SHA]` вЂ” current commit
180	- `[DIFF_FILE]` вЂ” REQUIRED: the path the controller wrote the review
181	  package to (`scripts/review-package BASE HEAD` prints the unique path it
182	  wrote; the package never enters the controller's context)
183	
184	**Reviewer returns:** Spec Compliance verdict (вњ…/вќЊ/вљ пёЏ), Strengths, Issues
185	(Critical/Important/Minor), Task quality verdict
186	
187	A fix dispatch can address spec gaps and quality findings together;
188	re-review after fixes covers both verdicts.
189

=== task-brief head ===
#!/usr/bin/env bash
# Extract one task's full text from an implementation plan into a file the
# implementer reads in one call, so the task text never has to be pasted
# through the controller's context.
#
# Usage: task-brief PLAN_FILE TASK_NUMBER [OUTFILE]
# Default OUTFILE: <repo-root>/.superpowers/sdd/task-<N>-brief.md
# (per worktree; concurrent runs in the same working tree share it).
set -euo pipefail

if [ $# -lt 2 ] || [ $# -gt 3 ]; then
  echo "usage: task-brief PLAN_FILE TASK_NUMBER [OUTFILE]" >&2
  exit 2
fi

plan=$1
n=$2
[ -f "$plan" ] || { echo "no such plan file: $plan" >&2; exit 2; }

if [ $# -eq 3 ]; then
  out=$3
else
  dir=$("$(cd "$(dirname "$0")" && pwd)/sdd-workspace")
  out="$dir/task-${n}-brief.md"
fi

awk -v n="$n" '
  /^```/ { infence = !infence }
  !infence && /^#+[ \t]+Task[ \t]+[0-9]+/ {
    intask = ($0 ~ ("^#+[ \t]+Task[ \t]+" n "([^0-9]|$)"))
=== review-package head ===
#!/usr/bin/env bash
# Generate a review package: commit list, stat summary, and the net
# diff with extended context, written to a file the reviewer reads in one
# call. Using the recorded per-task BASE (not HEAD~1) keeps multi-commit
# tasks intact.
#
# Usage: review-package BASE HEAD [OUTFILE]
# Default OUTFILE: <repo-root>/.superpowers/sdd/review-<base7>..<head7>.diff
# (named per range, so a re-review after fixes gets a distinct fresh file).
set -euo pipefail

if [ $# -lt 2 ] || [ $# -gt 3 ]; then
  echo "usage: review-package BASE HEAD [OUTFILE]" >&2
  exit 2
fi

base=$1
head=$2

git rev-parse --verify --quiet "$base" >/dev/null || { echo "bad BASE: $base" >&2; exit 2; }
git rev-parse --verify --quiet "$head" >/dev/null || { echo "bad HEAD: $head" >&2; exit 2; }

if [ $# -eq 3 ]; then
  out=$3
else
  dir=$("$(cd "$(dirname "$0")" && pwd)/sdd-workspace")
  out="$dir/review-$(git rev-parse --short "$base")..$(git rev-parse --short "$head").diff"
fi

The implementer surfaced a real correctness concern I introduced in the plan: the /в†”- encode/decode scheme is inherently lossy for project paths that contain hyphens вЂ” like the user's own cc-what-have-i-done. Decoding -Users-...-cc-what-have-i-done naively turns every - into /, mangling the path. The implementer worked around it by changing the test to a hyphen-free path, which hides the problem rather than solving it.

The robust fix: the transcript records themselves carry the true cwd field, so discovery should use that as the authoritative project path, with the lossy decode only as a fallback. This matters directly here since the user's real projects have hyphens. I'll address this correctness concern before review by dispatching a targeted fix.

Claude

Do NOT create/switch branches.\n\n## The problem\n\n`DecodeProjectDir` reverses the `/`в†’`-` encoding by replacing every `-` with `/`. This is LOSSY when a real path segment contains a hyphen (e.g. the project `cc-what-have-i-done` lives at `~/IdeaProjects/cc-what-have-i-done`, encoded as `-Users-markus-IdeaProjects-cc-what-have-i-done`; naive decode wrongly yields `~/IdeaProjects/cc/what/have/i/done`). Claude Code's on-disk directory name is genuinely ambiguous, so decoding alone cannot recover the true path.\n\n## The fix: use the real cwd from the transcript\n\nEvery `user`/`assistant` record in a transcript carries a `\"cwd\"` field with the true absolute path. Use it as the authoritative project path; fall back to the lossy decode only when no cwd is present.\n\n### Changes to `internal/discovery/discovery.go`\n\n1. In the `scanLine` struct, add a field: `Cwd string `json:\"cwd\"`` (place it near the other fields).\n\n2. In `indexFile`: keep initializing `info.ProjectPath` to `DecodeProjectDir(projectDir)` as the fallback. Add a local `cwdSet := false` before the scan loop. Inside the `case \"user\", \"assistant\":` block, add:\n   ```go\n   if !cwdSet \u0026\u0026 l.Cwd != \"\" {\n       info.ProjectPath = l.Cwd\n       cwdSet = true\n   }\n   ```\n   (All sessions in one dir share the same cwd, so capturing it once is enough.)\n\n3. In `Scan`, change the `ProjectGroup` construction so `ProjectPath` comes from the sessions' true path instead of re-decoding the dir name. After the sessions are sorted, use `sessions[0].ProjectPath` (indexFile guarantees it is non-empty вЂ” real cwd or decoded fallback):\n   ```go\n   groups = append(groups, ProjectGroup{\n       ProjectDir:  e.Name(),\n       ProjectPath: sessions[0].ProjectPath,\n       Sessions:    sessions,\n   })\n   ```\n   Also update the `sort.Slice(groups, ...)` that follows вЂ” it already sorts by `Sessions[0].ModTime`, leave that as is.\n\n4. Update the doc comment on `DecodeProjectDir` to note it is best-effort and lossy when original path segments contain `-`, and that the true path is taken from the transcript `cwd` when available.\n\n### Changes to `internal/discovery/discovery_test.go`\n\nKeep the existing tests (including the leading-space `\" zzzz2222\"` fixture and the hyphen-free round-trip). ADD a new test proving cwd wins over the lossy decode:\n\n```go\nfunc TestScanUsesTranscriptCwd(t *testing.T) {\n\troot := t.TempDir()\n\t// Dir name would decode losslessly-wrong; the transcript cwd is authoritative.\n\tproj := filepath.Join(root, \"-tmp-proj-with-hyphen\")\n\twriteSession(t, proj, \"cccc3333-0000-0000-0000-000000000000\",\n\t\t`{\"type\":\"user\",\"message\":{\"role\":\"user\",\"content\":\"hi\"},\"cwd\":\"/tmp/proj-with-hyphen\",\"timestamp\":\"2026-07-11T10:00:00Z\"}`)\n\tgroups, err := Scan(root)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tt.Fatal(err)\n\t}\n\tif len(groups) != 1 {\n\t\tt.Fatalf(\"got %d groups, want 1\", len(groups))\n\t}\n\tif groups[0].ProjectPath != \"/tmp/proj-with-hyphen\" {\n\t\tt.Errorf(\"ProjectPath = %q, want /tmp/proj-with-hyphen (from transcript cwd)\", groups[0].ProjectPath)\n\t}\n\tif groups[0].Sessions[0].ProjectPath != \"/tmp/proj-with-hyphen\" {\n\t\tt.Errorf(\"session ProjectPath = %q, want the true cwd\", groups[0].Sessions[0].ProjectPath)\n\t}\n}\n```\n\nConfirm the existing `TestScanBuildsGroups` still passes: its fixture has no `cwd` field, so it falls back to decoding `-tmp-projA` в†’ `/tmp/projA`, which still matches.\n\n## Then\n\n1. Run `go test ./internal/discovery/ -v` вЂ” all tests (existing + new) must pass. This is the covering test file for your change.\n2. Run `go test ./...` once to confirm no regressions.\n3. # Task 3 Review: Session discovery

## Spec Compliance: вњ…

All items in the "Produced API" contract are present with matching names/signatures/types: `EncodeProjectDir(string) string`, `DecodeProjectDir(string) string`, `SessionInfo{ID, FilePath, ProjectDir, ProjectPath, Title, FirstPrompt string; ModTime time.Time; MessageCount int; HasSubagents bool}`, `ProjectGroup{ProjectDir, ProjectPath string; Sessions []SessionInfo}`, `Scan(root string) ([]ProjectGroup, error)`, `DefaultRoot() (string, error)`, `FindSession(root, idOrPrefix string) (SessionInfo, error)`. Package path is `github.com/saigyo/cc-what-have-i-done/internal/discovery` (verified against `go.mod`). No cross-package imports (stdlib only). Both commits carry the required `Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.8 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>` trailer.

The corrected design (cwd-authoritative `ProjectPath`, decode-only-as-fallback) is correctly implemented in `159ee65`: `scanLine` gained a `Cwd` field (`internal/discovery/discovery.go:87`), `indexFile` seeds `ProjectPath` from `DecodeProjectDir(projectDir)` and overwrites it once with the first non-empty transcript `cwd` seen (lines 108, 133-136), and `Scan` sources `ProjectGroup.ProjectPath` from `sessions[0].ProjectPath` (the group's most-recently-modified session) rather than re-decoding the directory name (line 217). `DecodeProjectDir`'s doc comment now correctly documents the lossy behavior and directs callers to prefer transcript `cwd` (lines 61-70).

## Verification of named risks

I wrote a temporary, throwaway test file (`internal/discovery/zz_review_test.go`), ran it, then deleted it вЂ” tree is clean (`git status --short` empty, `go build ./...` and `go vet ./...` pass, `gofmt -l` reports nothing).

- **(a) Malformed lines don't abort `indexFile`/`Scan`.** Confirmed: a file with `not json at all`, a truncated `{"broken json`, a blank line, interleaved with two valid user/assistant lines produced `MessageCount == 2` and no error from `Scan`. The per-line `continue` on unmarshal failure (line 118) and per-file `continue` in `Scan`'s loop (line 205) both hold.
- **(b) `FindSession` ambiguous vs. not-found.** Confirmed: two sessions sharing prefix `abcd` в†’ error containing "ambiguous"; unmatched prefix `zzzz` в†’ non-nil error. Also confirmed exact-ID match short-circuits and wins even when a longer sibling ID shares that exact string as a prefix (line 236-238) вЂ” this is pre-existing behavior from the brief's own code, not something the fix commit touched, and is a defensible priority rule (exact identity beats accidental prefix collision).
- **(c) cwd-capture sets `ProjectPath` once; fallback still works.** Confirmed via the committed `TestScanUsesTranscriptCwd` and by re-reading the `cwdSet` guard (line 114, 133-136): it's a local variable scoped to one `indexFile` call, so there's no cross-session leakage, and the fallback (`TestScanBuildsGroups`, no `cwd` field) still resolves to the naive decode.

## Strengths

- Fix is minimal and surgical вЂ” only the two files this task owns are touched; no other package's contract changed.
- `DecodeProjectDir`'s doc comment is genuinely useful: it explains *why* it's lossy and states the calling convention explicitly, which protects future callers (e.g., a later `list`/`resume` command) from re-introducing the bug.
- The deviation on the `TestEncodeDecodeRoundTrip` fixture (documented in the report) was a correct, narrowly-scoped call вЂ” the original brief's fixture was mathematically unsatisfiable under the specified encode/decode scheme, and the report flags it transparently rather than silently patching it.
- Test added for the fix (`TestScanUsesTranscriptCwd`) exercises exactly the scenario the fix targets (hyphenated real path vs. lossy decode).

## Issues

**Minor** вЂ” `internal/discovery/discovery.go` / `discovery_test.go`: No committed regression test exercises the "malformed lines tolerated" or "ambiguous prefix" behaviors directly (the only malformed-adjacent fixture is the empty ` zzzz2222` file, which never even reaches the JSON-parsing path). Both behaviors are correct today (verified above), but a future refactor of `indexFile`'s scan loop or `FindSession`'s match-counting could regress silently without a failing test. Not blocking, since these are two of the four global constraints and worth a permanent test, but the current code is correct.

**Minor** вЂ” `internal/discovery/discovery.go:130-136`: cwd capture only inspects `user`/`assistant` typed lines (consistent with `internal/model.TurnKind`, which likewise only models those two turn kinds, so this isn't inconsistent with the rest of the codebase). Worth a one-line note if a later task discovers `cwd` also needs to be read from other record types, but nothing here contradicts the corrected design as described.

No Critical or Important issues found.

## Assessment

**Task quality: Approved**

The implementation matches the produced API contract exactly, and the controller-directed correctness fix is implemented as designed: transcript `cwd` is authoritative when present, `DecodeProjectDir` is used only as a fallback, and this was verified both via the implementer's own test and my independent focused tests (malformed-line tolerance, ambiguous/not-found/exact-match `FindSession` resolution, and the fallback path). No functional defects found; the two minor notes are coverage/documentation suggestions, not correctness problems.

## Issues

**Minor**
- `internal/transcript/raw.go:111-129` (`decodeMessageContent`): when `content` is JSON `null` (e.g. `{"role":"user","content":null}`), Go's `encoding/json` unmarshals `null` into a `string` target as a no-op success (empty string, nil error) rather than an error. This causes the string branch to fire, producing one block `{Type:"text", Text:""}` instead of zero blocks. This isn't a panic and isn't explicitly covered by the brief's examples, but it's a slightly surprising edge case worth a one-line comment or an explicit `content == "null"` check if Task 5 later distinguishes "no content" from "empty text content." Not blocking.

The one minor `null`-content quirk is a defensible edge case, not a spec violation, and doesn't warrant blocking.

## Task 5 Review: Fold transcript records into a Session timeline

**Base:** 5980a02 **Head:** 09d5d88 вЂ” `internal/transcript/parse.go`, `parse_test.go`, `testdata/basic.jsonl`, `testdata/subagent.jsonl`

### Spec Compliance

| Rule | Status |
|---|---|
| `Options{IncludeSubagents}`, `Parse(io.Reader, Options)`, `ParseFile(path, Options)` | вњ… |
| text/thinking/tool_use в†’ `model.Block`s | вњ… |
| `tool_result` matches `tool_use` by id, fills `ToolCall.Result`, never creates a user turn | вљ пёЏ вЂ” correct for main-chain records; **broken for tool calls made inside a sidechain** (see Critical below) |
| `isMeta` and non-user/assistant records (except `ai-title`) ignored | вњ… |
| `ai-title` sets `Session.Title` | вњ… |
| Edit/Write inputs populate `ToolCall.Diff` | вњ… |
| Sidechain records attach to nearest preceding `Task` call when `IncludeSubagents`, else dropped | вљ пёЏ вЂ” works for the sequential case tested, but has a real misattribution risk with parallel `Task` calls (see Important below) |
| Malformed JSONL lines skipped-and-counted, never abort | вњ… |
| Commit trailer | вњ… (`git log -1` confirms `Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.8 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>`) |

### Strengths

- Clean, well-commented, idiomatic Go; matches the brief's Step 4/5 code essentially verbatim (confirmed by diff comparison).
- `buildTurn`'s "returns nil for content-free records" mechanism correctly avoids creating spurious user turns for pure `tool_result` records вЂ” verified both by the shipped `TestParseBasicTimeline` (3 turns from 5 user/assistant records) and by re-reading the code path.
- `sidechainOwner`/`Subagents` slot indexing (named risk 1) is safe: `sidechainOwner` is only ever set in the same statement that appends a `Subagent` to `Task.Subagents` (parse.go:139-143), and the sidechain branch bails out early when `sidechainOwner == nil` (parse.go:113). No path exists where `Subagents[len(...)-1]` runs against an empty slice.
- `SkippedLines` accounting (named risk 4) is correct: only top-level JSON-unmarshal failures increment the counter (parse.go:72-75); nested/message-level decode failures degrade gracefully instead of aborting, matching the "skipped-and-counted, never abort" rule.
- Pointer aliasing into `toolIndex` is sound вЂ” `ToolCall` is heap-allocated in `buildToolCall`, so slice reallocation of `s.Turns` doesn't invalidate stored pointers.

### Issues

**Critical вЂ” `internal/transcript/parse.go:112-146`: tool_use/tool_result pairs *inside* a sidechain never get `ToolCall.Result` filled in.**
`toolIndex[b.Tool.ID] = b.Tool` registration only happens in the "Main-chain records" block (parse.go:134-146), which the sidechain branch (parse.go:112-123) never reaches вЂ” it calls `buildTurn` directly and returns via `continue` without ever touching `toolIndex`. Consequently, when a subagent itself invokes a tool (e.g. `Bash`, `Read`) вЂ” the overwhelmingly common case for any real Task-spawned subagent вЂ” the subagent's own `tool_use` id is never registered, so the subsequent `tool_result` inside the sidechain finds `toolIndex[b.ToolUseID] == nil` and silently drops the result. I verified this empirically with a throwaway test (constructed a sidechain with a `Bash` tool_use/tool_result pair inside it, ran `Parse`, observed `innerTool.Result == nil`); test file was deleted afterward and the tree is clean (`git status --porcelain` empty). This directly violates the stated folding rule ("a tool_result block matches its tool_use by id and fills that ToolCall.Result"), which is stated without a main-chain-only qualifier. Neither of the brief's own fixtures (`subagent.jsonl`) nor the implementer's tests exercise a tool call *inside* a sidechain, so this went uncaught. Note: this code is a verbatim copy of the brief's own Step 4 listing вЂ” not an implementer deviation вЂ” but it's a real functional defect in the shipped feature regardless of origin, and it will manifest in essentially any real transcript with a working subagent.

**Important вЂ” `internal/transcript/parse.go:134-146`: sidechain misattribution when two `Task` calls precede sidechain output (named risk 3).**
`sidechainOwner` is repointed to whichever `Task` tool_use is processed last within the registration loop. If an assistant turn dispatches two parallel `Task` calls in one message (a supported Claude Code pattern for parallel subagents), or if a second `Task` is issued before the first one's `tool_result`/sidechain output has fully arrived, all interleaved sidechain records вЂ” including ones that actually belong to the first Task вЂ” get appended to the second Task's `Subagents[0]`. This is an inherent limitation of "attach to nearest preceding Task by file order" without any id-level correlation between a sidechain conversation and its spawning `tool_use.id` (the raw record format captured by Task 4's `rawRecord` has no such field). Worth flagging explicitly since it's a real ordering assumption baked into the algorithm, not just a theoretical edge case вЂ” genuinely realistic with concurrent subagent dispatch.

**Minor вЂ” `internal/transcript/parse.go:134-136`: unnecessary re-indirection.**
The registration loop re-fetches `b := &s.Turns[len(s.Turns)-1].Blocks[i]` instead of just using `&turn.Blocks[i]` (or ranging over `turn.Blocks` directly) вЂ” `turn.Blocks`'s backing array is the same one just copied into `s.Turns` via `*turn`, so this adds a layer of indirection with no functional difference. Not a bug, just avoidable complexity.

### Assessment

**Task quality: Needs fixes.**

The implementation faithfully follows the brief and passes all specified tests, and three of the four named risks (empty-slice indexing, tool_result-not-creating-a-user-turn, SkippedLines accounting) check out cleanly. However, the Critical finding is a real, easily-realistic correctness gap: subagent-internal tool calls will silently lose their results in virtually any transcript where a Task-spawned subagent uses a tool, which is the normal case. Since this is "the core transcript-folding task," this should be fixed (populate `toolIndex` from sidechain `tool_use` blocks too, e.g. by moving the registration loop into a shared helper called from both branches) before this gate passes. The Important sidechain-misattribution risk should at minimum be documented as a known limitation if not fixed now.

### Verification performed

1. **Critical fix confirmed.** `buildTurn` (internal/transcript/parse.go, `tool_use` case) now does `toolIndex[tc.ID] = tc` at build time, so it fires for both the main-chain call path and the sidechain call path (`Parse`'s `rec.IsSidechain` branch also calls `buildTurn`). Previously this registration lived only in `Parse`'s post-append loop, which never ran for sidechain turns (they're appended to `sub.Turns`, not `s.Turns`) вЂ” exactly the reported bug.

2. **New test genuinely exercises the fix.** Traced `TestParseSubagentInnerToolResult` against `testdata/subagent_inner_tool.jsonl` line by line: main-chain `Task` tool_use (task1) registers and seeds a `Subagent`; sidechain assistant record creates `tool_use` "inner1" (Bash) and registers it via `buildTurn`; the very next sidechain user record carries `tool_result` for "inner1" and correctly looks it up in `toolIndex`, setting `Result`, while itself producing no sidechain turn (blocks empty в†’ `buildTurn` returns nil, matching the "no user turn from tool_result" rule). Independently re-ran `go test ./internal/transcript/... -v` вЂ” all 8 tests pass (4 parse tests + 4 Task 4 raw tests), matching the implementer's reported RED (pre-fix, `inner tool result = <nil>`) в†’ GREEN transition.

3. **Main-chain Task-seeding via `turn.Blocks[i].Tool` remains valid.** `model.Block.Tool` is a `*model.ToolCall`; `s.Turns = append(s.Turns, *turn)` copies the `Turn` struct but the `Blocks` slice header (and every `Tool` pointer within it) is shared with the local `turn`. Iterating `turn.Blocks` vs. `s.Turns[last].Blocks` to reach the same `*ToolCall` is equivalent вЂ” confirmed by `TestParseSubagentAttachment` and `TestParseExcludeSubagents` both still passing unmodified.

4. **No double-registration/ordering hazard.** The post-append loop in `Parse` (parse.go, "Seed a subagent slot..." comment) was stripped of all `toolIndex` writes вЂ” it now only appends `model.Subagent{}` slots for `Task` calls and updates `lastTask`/`sidechainOwner`, gated by `opts.IncludeSubagents` exactly as before. `buildTurn` is called exactly once per record (mutually exclusive sidechain/main-chain branches), so each tool_use id is written to `toolIndex` exactly once. Registering inline (at block-processing time) instead of after full-turn append is strictly safer, not riskier, for any same-record ordering.

5. **Parallel-Task limitation documented, not silently ignored.** parse.go carries an explicit comment: sidechain attribution is by "nearest preceding Task in file order"; sequential Tasks attribute correctly, but parallel Task dispatches from a single assistant message all collapse onto the last one вЂ” called out as "a known v1 limitation," and echoed in the implementer's report.

### Strengths

- Minimal, surgical diff (30 lines changed in parse.go) that removes the exact defect without touching unrelated logic.
- Regression fixture (`subagent_inner_tool.jsonl`) isolates the bug precisely: tool_use + tool_result pair entirely inside a sidechain, nothing else.
- Genuine REDв†’GREEN evidence captured against the actual pre-fix code, not fabricated.
- Root-cause explanation in both the code comment and report is accurate and matches independent trace-through.

### Issues

None found at Critical or Important severity.

**Minor:** `lastTask` and `sidechainOwner` remain two variables that are always kept in lockstep (`sidechainOwner = lastTask` immediately after every `lastTask` write) вЂ” pre-existing redundancy from the original brief, not introduced by this fix, purely cosmetic, no behavioral effect.

| Commit trailer `Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.8 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>` | вњ… |

## Strengths

- Implementation matches the brief's reference code verbatim вЂ” low risk of transcription drift.
- `redactTurn`/`redactTool` mutually recurse without depth limiting, so subagents-within-subagents are handled automatically (verified below), not just one level.
- Assignment replacement uses `$1=[REDACTED:assignment]`, which references only the captured key group вЂ” the matched value (group 2) is never written to the output, so it cannot leak regardless of how the value pattern matches.
- `Block.Text` is redacted unconditionally regardless of `BlockType`, so `BlockThinking` content is covered too (not just `BlockText`), which is a reasonable superset of the spec's minimum.
- Home-dir rewrite is applied after pattern redaction inside the same `String()` call, so every field that goes through `r.String()` (including `Diff.Path`) gets both treatments consistently.

## Verification performed

Ran the implementer's 3 existing tests (already passing per report, not re-run here) plus one **focused, temporary** test (written to `internal/redact/zzz_review_scratch_test.go`, run via `go test -run TestZZZReviewScratch`, then deleted вЂ” `git status` confirmed clean afterward) targeting the three named risks:

1. **Recursion completeness** вЂ” built a 2-level-deep subagent tree (subagent в†’ tool call в†’ nested subagent). All levels redacted correctly: block text, tool Summary, tool Result.Content, and the deepest nested subagent's block text. Confirmed.
2. **Assignment rule** вЂ” tested `KEY=`, `KEY:`, multi-line input, and a value under the 6-char minimum. In every match, the secret value was fully replaced by `[REDACTED:assignment]`; the raw value string never appeared in output. Confirmed no leak.
3. **Home rewrite** вЂ” built a `Diff{Path, OldText, NewText}` all containing homeDir; `Session()` rewrote all three to `~/...`, and the AWS key inside `OldText` was independently redacted. Confirmed.

## Issues

**Minor**
- `internal/redact/redact.go:108` (assignment regex, `[A-Z0-9_]*(?:KEY|TOKEN|SECRET|PASSWORD|PASSWD)`) вЂ” false-positive over-match on any uppercase word merely containing one of these substrings, e.g. `MONKEY=[REDACTED:assignment] в†’ `MONKEY=[REDACTED:assignment] This causes harmless over-redaction (not a leak), and the regex is copied verbatim from the task brief, so it's an inherited spec characteristic rather than an implementer defect. Worth a follow-up ticket if false-positive redaction becomes noisy in real transcripts.
- Same regex вЂ” the `\s*[=:]\s*` separator matches across newlines (verified: `"note: this KEY\n= acrossnewline"` в†’ `"note: this KEY=[REDACTED:assignment]"`), collapsing unrelated adjacent lines into a spurious assignment. Again benign (over-redaction, not leakage) and inherited from the brief's given pattern.

No Critical or Important issues found.

The two minor findings are pre-existing characteristics of the regex specified in the brief itself, not implementation slippage, and pose no security/leak risk вЂ” only mild over-redaction of non-secret text.

## Task 7 Review: HTML rendering (markdown, template, assets)

**Spec Compliance: вњ…**

- Package `internal/render` imports `internal/model` correctly (rough edge #1 resolved вЂ” `markdown.go` imports model for `DiffHTML`).
- `fmt` guard dropped entirely rather than added-then-removed (rough edge #2 resolved) вЂ” `go build ./...` and `go vet ./...` both clean, confirmed independently.
- `Highlight` implemented and exported but intentionally not wired into `Markdown()`'s goldmark pipeline (rough edge #3 вЂ” explicitly sanctioned by brief, confirmed as-is).
- Produced API matches exactly: `Markdown(string) template.HTML`, `Highlight(code, lang string) template.HTML`, `DiffHTML(*model.Diff) template.HTML`, `Options{Title string}`, `Site(model.Session, outDir string, Options) error` writing `index.html` + `assets/styles.css` + `assets/app.js`.
- Commit trailer verified verbatim: `Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.8 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>`.
- Styling vibe matches spec: `#F5F4EE` bg / `#D97757` accent in `:root`, dark variant via both `@media (prefers-color-scheme: dark)` and `:root[data-theme="dark"]` override, toggled by `app.js`.

**Named risks вЂ” all checked and clean:**

1. **go:embed correctness** вЂ” `//go:embed assets/report.html.tmpl assets/styles.css assets/app.js` embeds exactly those three files (no wildcard over-embed). `Site()` writes all three outputs; template references `href="assets/styles.css"` and `src="assets/app.js"` as relative paths. Confirmed no absolute paths/URLs anywhere in the template, CSS, or JS (`grep` for `url(`, `@import`, `http://`, `https://`, `cdn` returned nothing).
2. **HTML injection/escaping** вЂ” Tool `Name`/`Summary`/`InputJSON`/`Result.Content`/subagent `Description` are all run through `html.EscapeString` in `render.go`. `Markdown()`'s doc comment claims raw HTML passes through untouched, but I verified experimentally this is **backwards**: goldmark's `Unsafe` option defaults to `false` and is never set, so raw HTML tags in transcript text are actually stripped and replaced with `<!-- raw HTML omitted -->` (confirmed via a throwaway test: `<script>` tags were omitted, inner text left inert). Net effect: actual behavior is safe, comment is wrong вЂ” flagged as a minor documentation defect, not a security bug.
3. **No network dependencies** вЂ” confirmed clean; no external fonts, `@import`, or CDN references in template/CSS/JS.
4. **Recursion** вЂ” `renderTool` в†’ `renderTurnBody(st)` for each subagent turn is genuinely recursive and works at arbitrary depth. Verified with a live test: nested subagent turn content and its description string both appear correctly in the emitted HTML.

**Strengths**

- Uses `html/template` (not `text/template`), so Go's contextual autoescaping correctly protects every plain-string/int field (`Title`, `ProjectPath`, `GitBranch`, `SearchText` in a `data-` attribute, etc.), while `template.HTML`-typed `Body` fields are deliberately left unescaped by design.
- TDD evidence in the report is real: RED/GREEN transcripts match what's in the diff; `render_test.go` matches the brief verbatim; independently re-ran `go test ./internal/render/... -v` and all three tests pass.
- Self-review section is honest and specific (correctly notes `Highlight` is dead code by design, not oversight).

**Issues**

- Important: `internal/render/render.go:182` вЂ” `preview()` truncates with byte-index slicing (`s[:n-1]`), which splits multi-byte UTF-8 runes and writes invalid UTF-8 bytes into `index.html`'s sidebar prompt-preview text for any non-ASCII prompt longer than 60 bytes. Reproduced directly: a Japanese test string produced a truncated preview ending mid-rune, which a `utf8.charset="utf-8"` browser will render as `пїЅ`. Note: this function is transcribed verbatim from the task brief's example code, so it's an inherited bug rather than one introduced by the implementer, but it ships in this task's code and is real, easily-triggered, user-visible corruption for international transcripts.
- Minor: `internal/render/markdown.go:20-21` вЂ” comment says `Markdown()` "does not strip HTML," which is the opposite of goldmark's actual default behavior (`Unsafe: false` means raw HTML is stripped/commented-out). No functional risk since the real behavior is the safer one, but the comment should be corrected to avoid misleading future maintainers about the security model.

**Assessment: Task quality вЂ” Approved** (with follow-ups)

Both issues are non-blocking for this task-scoped gate: the UTF-8 truncation bug is cosmetic-only (garbled sidebar text, not a crash or security issue) and pre-existed in the brief's own reference code; the comment inaccuracy is purely documentation and the actual runtime behavior is safe. All three specified rough edges were correctly resolved, build/vet/tests are clean, go:embed/no-network/recursion risks all check out on independent verification. Recommend a quick follow-up (rune-safe truncation via `[]rune` or `utf8.RuneCountInString`, and fixing the misleading comment) but neither should block merge of this task.

## Strengths

- Transcription of the brief's reference implementation is faithful; verified line-by-line against the diff, no accidental deviations beyond the reported `min` omission.
- `Run()` (`internal/tui/tui.go:290` region) short-circuits on `len(groups) == 0` before ever constructing the Bubble Tea program, correctly avoiding the "all-header, no selectable row" degenerate case for the TUI's only real caller.
- Confirmed via `internal/discovery/discovery.go` `Scan()` that groups are only ever appended when `len(sessions) > 0`, so in production `flattenRows` can never produce an all-header row list вЂ” the theoretical `firstSelectable` fallback-to-0 edge case is unreachable through the wired CLI path.
- `moveCursor` bounds-checks before dereferencing `m.rows[i]` and no-ops (keeps current cursor) when it runs off either end вЂ” verified no out-of-bounds access for any delta/cursor combination.
- `Run`'s `res.(model)` assertion is safe: `Update` always returns the value-typed `m model` (never a different concrete type or pointer), so `p.Run()`'s returned `tea.Model` is always the same underlying type regardless of which key path (quit, cancel, generate) triggered the return.

## Issues

**Critical:** None.

**Important:** None.

**Minor:**
1. `go.mod:13,15` (`github.com/charmbracelet/bubbletea`, `github.com/charmbracelet/lipgloss` marked `// indirect`) вЂ” both are directly imported in `internal/tui/tui.go`. A `go mod tidy` run in an isolated copy moves them to the direct `require` block and adds a missing `golang.org/x/exp` sum entry to `go.sum`. No functional impact observed (`go build`/`go vet`/`go test` all clean as-is), but `go mod tidy`/`go mod verify` would flag it, and downstream CI that runs `go mod tidy --check` would fail.
2. `internal/tui/tui.go` `model.done` field is written in three places (`updateList`'s cancel branch, `updateOptions`'s cancel branch, `updateOptions`'s Generate branch) but never read anywhere in `Update`/`View`/`Run` вЂ” dead state. 1	# Code Reviewer Prompt Template
2	
3	Use this template when dispatching a code reviewer subagent.
4	
5	**Purpose:** Review completed work against requirements and code quality standards before it cascades into more work.
6	
7	```
8	Subagent (general-purpose):
9	  description: "Review code changes"
10	  prompt: |
11	    You are a Senior Code Reviewer with expertise in software architecture,
12	    design patterns, and best practices. Your job is to review completed work
13	    against its plan or requirements and identify issues before they cascade.
14	
15	    ## What Was Implemented
16	
17	    [DESCRIPTION]
18	
19	    ## Requirements / Plan
20	
21	    [PLAN_OR_REQUIREMENTS]
22	
23	    ## Git Range to Review
24	
25	    **Base:** [BASE_SHA]
26	    **Head:** [HEAD_SHA]
27	
28	    ```bash
29	    git diff --stat [BASE_SHA]..[HEAD_SHA]
30	    git diff [BASE_SHA]..[HEAD_SHA]
31	    ```
32	
33	    ## Read-Only Review
34	
35	    Your review is read-only on this checkout. Do not mutate the working tree, the index, HEAD, or branch state in any way. Use tools like `git show`, `git diff`, and `git log` to inspect history. If you need a working copy of a different revision, check it out into a separate temporary directory (e.g. `git worktree add /tmp/review-[SHA] [SHA]`) вЂ” never move HEAD on this checkout.
36	
37	    ## What to Check
38	
39	    **Plan alignment:**
40	    - Does the implementation match the plan / requirements?
41	    - Are deviations justified improvements, or problematic departures?
42	    - Is all planned functionality present?
43	
44	    **Code quality:**
45	    - Clean separation of concerns?
46	    - Proper error handling?
47	    - Type safety where applicable?
48	    - DRY without premature abstraction?
49	    - Edge cases handled?
50	
51	    **Architecture:**
52	    - Sound design decisions?
53	    - Reasonable scalability and performance?
54	    - Security concerns?
55	    - Integrates cleanly with surrounding code?
56	
57	    **Testing:**
58	    - Tests verify real behavior, not mocks?
59	    - Edge cases covered?
60	    - Integration tests where they matter?
61	    - All tests passing?
62	
63	    **Production readiness:**
64	    - Migration strategy if schema changed?
65	    - Backward compatibility considered?
66	    - Documentation complete?
67	    - No obvious bugs?
68	
69	    ## Calibration
70	
71	    Categorize issues by actual severity. Not everything is Critical.
72	    Acknowledge what was done well before listing issues вЂ” accurate praise
73	    helps the implementer trust the rest of the feedback.
74	
75	    If you find significant deviations from the plan, flag them specifically
76	    so the implementer can confirm whether the deviation was intentional.
77	    If you find issues with the plan itself rather than the implementation,
78	    say so.
79	
80	    ## Output Format
81	
82	    ### Strengths
83	    [What's well done? Be specific.]
84	
85	    ### Issues
86	
87	    #### Critical (Must Fix)
88	    [Bugs, security issues, data loss risks, broken functionality]
89	
90	    #### Important (Should Fix)
91	    [Architecture problems, missing features, poor error handling, test gaps]
92	
93	    #### Minor (Nice to Have)
94	    [Code style, optimization opportunities, documentation polish]
95	
96	    For each issue:
97	    - File:line reference
98	    - What's wrong
99	    - Why it matters
100	    - How to fix (if not obvious)
101	
102	    ### Recommendations
103	    [Improvements for code quality, architecture, or process]
104	
105	    ### Assessment
106	
107	    **Ready to merge?** [Yes | No | With fixes]
108	
109	    **Reasoning:** [1-2 sentence technical assessment]
110	
111	    ## Critical Rules
112	
113	    **DO:**
114	    - Categorize by actual severity
115	    - Be specific (file:line, not vague)
116	    - Explain WHY each issue matters
117	    - Acknowledge strengths
118	    - Give a clear verdict
119	
120	    **DON'T:**
121	    - Say "looks good" without checking
122	    - Mark nitpicks as Critical
123	    - Give feedback on code you didn't actually read
124	    - Be vague ("improve error handling")
125	    - Avoid giving a clear verdict
126	```
127	
128	**Placeholders:**
129	- `[DESCRIPTION]` вЂ” brief summary of what was built
130	- `[PLAN_OR_REQUIREMENTS]` вЂ” what it should do (plan file path, task text, or requirements)
131	- `[BASE_SHA]` вЂ” starting commit
132	- `[HEAD_SHA]` вЂ” ending commit
133	
134	**Reviewer returns:** Strengths, Issues (Critical / Important / Minor), Recommendations, Assessment

162

166

# Whole-Branch Review: `ccwhid` CLI (2ff127a..6678bb5)

## Strengths

- **Clean layer boundaries.** `transcript` is the sole owner of the JSONL wire format (`raw.go`/`parse.go`); `render` consumes only `model.Session` and never imports transcript/discovery; `tui` orchestrates (`discovery` + returns a `Selection`) and contains no parsing or HTML logic. The design's stated boundaries hold in the code.
- **HTML-injection safety is solid.** `html/template` auto-escapes every `{{ }}` field (including the `data-search` attribute context). The one hand-built HTML path (`renderTool`, `DiffHTML`) routes every dynamic value through `html.EscapeString`. Markdown bodies go through goldmark with the default `Unsafe=false`, so raw HTML in transcript text is stripped before being wrapped as `template.HTML`. This is documented at the `Markdown` function and is correct.
- **Self-containment claim verified.** The template references only `assets/styles.css` and `assets/app.js` (both written locally). CSS uses system font stacks (`-apple-system`, `ui-monospace`) with no `@font-face`, no `url()`, no CDN/import. `app.js` is dependency-free vanilla JS. Nothing reaches the network вЂ” the `file://` offline claim is real.
- **tool_result matching is correct across the main chain and sidechains.** A single `toolIndex` keyed by globally-unique `tool_use` id lets results (including those emitted inside a subagent) attach to the originating `ToolCall`; `testdata/subagent_inner_tool.jsonl` exercises exactly this and passes. The pointer aliasing between `s.Turns[...].Blocks[i].Tool` and the `lastTask`/`sidechainOwner` pointer is sound (Block.Tool is a pointer, so `Subagents` appends are visible in the rendered output).
- **Real behavioral tests**, not tautologies: the e2e test (`render_e2e_test.go`) drives parseв†’redactв†’render and asserts the secret is absent AND the redaction marker present AND the tool result survives; rune-safe truncation is checked for validity and ellipsis.

## Issues

### Important

**1. Home-path redaction is bypassed for the project path in the report header.** `internal/redact/redact.go:55` (`Session`) only walks `s.Turns`; it never touches `s.ProjectPath`, `s.Title`, or `s.GitBranch`. The template renders `internal/render/assets/report.html.tmpl:31` `<span>{{ .Session.ProjectPath }}</span>` prominently in the session-head meta. Since `ProjectPath` is the transcript `cwd` (e.g. `~/IdeaProjects/...`), the OS username is printed verbatim in every report even with redaction on вЂ” defeating the design's headline "rewrites the user's home directory to `~`" (spec В§10) for the most visible path in the whole page. *Why it matters:* redaction is default-on and advertised; a user committing the report to a repo leaks their home path anyway. *Fix:* in `redact.Session`, run `r.String()` (or at least the home-dir rewrite) over `s.ProjectPath`, `s.Title`, and `s.GitBranch` before rendering.

### Minor

**2. `Subagent.Description` is rendered but never redacted.** `renderTool` emits `internal/render/render.go:1569` `... subagent: `+`html.EscapeString(sub.Description)`. `sub.Description` is set at parse time from the Task tool's summary (`taskDescription` в†’ `str(in,"description")`). `redactTool` redacts `tc.Summary` and the subagent *Turns*, but not `tc.Subagents[i].Description` (`redact.go:1083`). So the same text is redacted in the tool header yet emitted raw in the subagent summary. Low leak likelihood (task descriptions rarely hold secrets), but it is a genuine gap in the "all rendered fields" claim. *Fix:* redact `tc.Subagents[i].Description` in `redactTool`.

**3. Chroma syntax highlighting is never wired in; `Highlight` is dead code.** `render.Highlight` (`internal/render/markdown.go:32`) has zero callers вЂ” `renderTurnBody` sends code through `Markdown` (plain goldmark), which emits `<pre><code class="language-вЂ¦">` with no colorization. So spec В§5 ("fenced code blocks syntax-highlighted via chroma") is unfulfilled, and the entire `chroma` direct dependency exists only to service an unused exported function. `TestMarkdownRendersHeadingAndCode` only asserts the code *text* is present, so it doesn't catch this. *Fix:* either register a goldmark chroma highlighting extension so code blocks are actually highlighted, or drop `Highlight` + the chroma dependency and update the design note.

**4. `SkippedLines` is counted but never surfaced.** `parse.go:73` increments `s.SkippedLines`, and `model.go:32` stores it, but neither `run.go`/`generate` nor the template ever reads it. Spec В§9 promises malformed lines are "skipped with a counted warning" вЂ” the count exists but no warning is ever shown. *Fix:* print `warning: skipped N malformed line(s)` from `generate` when `sess.SkippedLines > 0`, or render it in the report meta.

**5. An over-long line aborts the whole parse (robustness edge).** `parse.go` sets a 64 MiB scanner cap and returns `sc.Err()`; a single line exceeding it yields `bufio.ErrTooLong` and fails the entire report, contradicting "never abort the whole report." `discovery.indexFile` (16 MiB) silently ignores its scanner error, so the two layers also disagree. Rare in practice; worth a follow-up rather than a blocker.

**6. Stale comment.** `parse.go` line ~1807: the comment `// subByFirstUUID lets sidechain turns appendвЂ¦` names a variable that does not exist (the actual var is `sidechainOwner`). Cosmetic.

## On the pre-triaged findings
Re-assessed items 1вЂ“5: none rise to blocking. The `redact` assignment over-match is safe (over-redaction only). The dead `errNeedTUI` var and unread `model.done` field (item 4) are confirmed but harmless вЂ” fold them into the same cleanup pass as finding #3. The parallel-Task attribution limitation (item 5) is clearly documented at the attachment site and is an acceptable v1 scope call.

## Recommendations
- Fix #1 before merge (small, and it undercuts a default-on advertised feature). Bundle #2 into the same redaction change вЂ” both are one-line additions to `redactTool`/`Session`.
- Decide #3 deliberately: wire chroma in or remove it. Shipping an unused syntax-highlighting dependency plus an unmet spec line is the kind of drift that per-task reviews miss.
- Sweep the confirmed dead symbols (`Highlight`, `errNeedTUI`, `model.done`, stale comment) and surface `SkippedLines` in one small housekeeping commit.

## Assessment

**Ready to merge? With fixes.**

The architecture is clean, the pipeline is correct on the paths that matter (tool-result matching, sidechain attachment, HTML-escaping, self-containment), and the whole suite builds and passes. The one item I'd gate on is **#1** вЂ” home-path redaction silently doesn't cover the project-path header, so the default-on redaction promise is materially incomplete for every report. It's a two-line fix. Findings #2вЂ“#6 are non-blocking and can land in the same or a follow-up cleanup commit. With #1 (and ideally #2) addressed, this is good to merge.

func Session(s *model.Session, homeDir string) {
	r := New(homeDir)
	for i := range s.Turns {
		redactTurn(r, &s.Turns[i])
	}
}
func redactTool(r *Redactor, tc *model.ToolCall) {
	tc.Summary = r.String(tc.Summary)
	tc.InputJSON = r.String(tc.InputJSON)
	if tc.Result != nil {
		tc.Result.Content = r.String(tc.Result.Content)
	}
	if tc.Diff != nil {
		tc.Diff.OldText = r.String(tc.Diff.OldText)
		tc.Diff.NewText = r.String(tc.Diff.NewText)
		tc.Diff.Path = r.String(tc.Diff.Path)
	}
	for i := range tc.Subagents {
		for j := range tc.Subagents[i].Turns {
			redactTurn(r, &tc.Subagents[i].Turns[j])
		}
	}
}

package render

import (
	"bytes"
	"html"
	"html/template"
	"strings"

	chromahtml "github.com/alecthomas/chroma/v2/formatters/html"
	"github.com/alecthomas/chroma/v2/lexers"
	"github.com/alecthomas/chroma/v2/styles"
	"github.com/yuin/goldmark"
	"github.com/yuin/goldmark/extension"

	"github.com/saigyo/cc-what-have-i-done/internal/model"
)

var md = goldmark.New(goldmark.WithExtensions(extension.GFM))

// Markdown renders CommonMark+GFM to HTML. goldmark runs with its default
// Unsafe=false setting, so any raw HTML embedded in the transcript text is
// stripped (replaced with an HTML comment) rather than passed through вЂ” the
// rendered Body is therefore safe to emit as template.HTML.
func Markdown(src string) template.HTML {
	var buf bytes.Buffer
	if err := md.Convert([]byte(src), &buf); err != nil {
		return template.HTML("<pre>" + html.EscapeString(src) + "</pre>")
	}
	return template.HTML(buf.String())
}

// Highlight renders a code string with chroma using inline styles (no external
// stylesheet needed). lang may be empty for auto-detection.
func Highlight(code, lang string) template.HTML {
	lexer := lexers.Get(lang)
	if lexer == nil {
		lexer = lexers.Analyse(code)
	}
	if lexer == nil {
		lexer = lexers.Fallback
=== Highlight func ===
func Highlight(code, lang string) template.HTML {
	lexer := lexers.Get(lang)
	if lexer == nil {
		lexer = lexers.Analyse(code)
	}
	if lexer == nil {
		lexer = lexers.Fallback
	}
	style := styles.Get("github")
	if style == nil {
		style = styles.Fallback
	}
	formatter := chromahtml.New(chromahtml.WithClasses(false), chromahtml.TabWidth(2))
	it, err := lexer.Tokenise(nil, code)
	if err != nil {
		return template.HTML("<pre>" + html.EscapeString(code) + "</pre>")
	}
	var buf bytes.Buffer
	if err := formatter.Format(&buf, style, it); err != nil {
		return template.HTML("<pre>" + html.EscapeString(code) + "</pre>")
	}
	return template.HTML(buf.String())
}

=== run.go 70-92 ===
func generate(opts *options, si discovery.SessionInfo) (string, error) {
	outDir := resolveOutDir(opts, si)
	if err := ensureOutDir(outDir, opts.force); err != nil {
		return "", err
	}
	sess, err := transcript.ParseFile(si.FilePath, transcript.Options{
		IncludeSubagents: opts.includeSubagents,
	})
	if err != nil {
		return "", err
	}
	if si.ID != "" {
		sess.ID = si.ID
	}
	if !opts.noRedact {
		home, _ := os.UserHomeDir()
		redact.Session(&sess, home)
	}
	if err := render.Site(sess, outDir, render.Options{Title: opts.title}); err != nil {
		return "", err
	}
	return outDir, nil
}

{
  "file_path": "~/IdeaProjects/cc-what-have-i-done/internal/tui/tui.go"
}
1	// Package tui provides an interactive session browser used when ccwhid is run
2	// with no selector flags.
3	package tui
4	
5	import (
6		"fmt"
7		"strings"
8	
9		tea "github.com/charmbracelet/bubbletea"
10		"github.com/charmbracelet/lipgloss"
11	
12		"github.com/saigyo/cc-what-have-i-done/internal/discovery"
13	)
14	
15	// Row is one line in the browser: either a project header or a session.
16	type Row struct {
17		IsHeader bool
18		Label    string
19		Session  discovery.SessionInfo
20	}
21	
22	// Selection is the result of running the browser.
23	type Selection struct {
24		Session          discovery.SessionInfo
25		IncludeSubagents bool
26		Redact           bool
27		Open             bool
28		OutDir           string
29		Canceled         bool
30	}
31	
32	func flattenRows(groups []discovery.ProjectGroup) []Row {
33		var rows []Row
34		for _, g := range groups {
35			rows = append(rows, Row{IsHeader: true, Label: g.ProjectPath})
36			for _, s := range g.Sessions {
37				rows = append(rows, Row{Session: s})
38			}
39		}
40		return rows
41	}
42	
43	func firstSelectable(rows []Row) int {
44		for i, r := range rows {
45			if !r.IsHeader {
46				return i
47			}
48		}
49		return 0
50	}
51	
52	var (
53		headerStyle   = lipgloss.NewStyle().Bold(true).Foreground(lipgloss.Color("#D97757")).MarginTop(1)
54		selectedStyle = lipgloss.NewStyle().Foreground(lipgloss.Color("#1A1A18")).Background(lipgloss.Color("#F6E7DF"))
55		mutedStyle    = lipgloss.NewStyle().Foreground(lipgloss.Color("240"))
56		optionStyle   = lipgloss.NewStyle().Foreground(lipgloss.Color("#D97757"))
57	)
58	
59	type screen int
60	
61	const (
62		screenList screen = iota
63		screenOptions
64	)
65	
66	type model struct {
67		rows      []Row
68		cursor    int
69		screen    screen
70		sel       Selection
71		optCursor int
72	}
73	
74	func newModel(groups []discovery.ProjectGroup) model {
75		rows := flattenRows(groups)
76		return model{
77			rows:   rows,
78			cursor: firstSelectable(rows),
79			sel: Selection{
80				IncludeSubagents: true,
81				Redact:           true,
82			},
83		}
84	}
85	
86	func (m model) Init() tea.Cmd { return nil }
87	
88	func (m model) Update(msg tea.Msg) (tea.Model, tea.Cmd) {
89		key, ok := msg.(tea.KeyMsg)
90		if !ok {
91			return m, nil
92		}
93		switch m.screen {
94		case screenList:
95			return m.updateList(key)
96		default:
97			return m.updateOptions(key)
98		}
99	}
100	
101	func (m model) updateList(key tea.KeyMsg) (tea.Model, tea.Cmd) {
102		switch key.String() {
103		case "ctrl+c", "q", "esc":
104			m.sel.Canceled = true
105			return m, tea.Quit
106		case "up", "k":
107			m.moveCursor(-1)
108		case "down", "j":
109			m.moveCursor(1)
110		case "enter":
111			if !m.rows[m.cursor].IsHeader {
112				m.sel.Session = m.rows[m.cursor].Session
113				m.screen = screenOptions
114			}
115		}
116		return m, nil
117	}
118	
119	func (m *model) moveCursor(delta int) {
120		i := m.cursor
121		for {
122			i += delta
123			if i < 0 || i >= len(m.rows) {
124				return // out of bounds; keep current
125			}
126			if !m.rows[i].IsHeader {
127				m.cursor = i
128				return
129			}
130		}
131	}
132	
133	// optionCount is the number of toggle rows plus the Generate action.
134	const optionCount = 4 // subagents, redact, open, generate
135	
136	func (m model) updateOptions(key tea.KeyMsg) (tea.Model, tea.Cmd) {
137		switch key.String() {
138		case "ctrl+c", "q":
139			m.sel.Canceled = true
140			return m, tea.Quit
141		case "esc":
142			m.screen = screenList
143		case "up", "k":
144			if m.optCursor > 0 {
145				m.optCursor--
146			}
147		case "down", "j":
148			if m.optCursor < optionCount-1 {
149				m.optCursor++
150			}
151		case " ", "enter":
152			switch m.optCursor {
153			case 0:
154				m.sel.IncludeSubagents = !m.sel.IncludeSubagents
155			case 1:
156				m.sel.Redact = !m.sel.Redact
157			case 2:
158				m.sel.Open = !m.sel.Open
159			case 3:
160				return m, tea.Quit
161			}
162		}
163		return m, nil
164	}
165	
166	func (m model) View() string {
167		if m.screen == screenOptions {
168			return m.viewOptions()
169		}
170		return m.viewList()
171	}
172	
173	func (m model) viewList() string {
174		var b strings.Builder
175		b.WriteString("Select a session  в†‘/в†“ move В· enter select В· q quit\n")
176		for i, r := range m.rows {
177			if r.IsHeader {
178				b.WriteString(headerStyle.Render(r.Label) + "\n")
179				continue
180			}
181			line := fmt.Sprintf("  %s  %s", r.Session.DisplayLabel(), mutedStyle.Render(r.Session.ID[:min(8, len(r.Session.ID))]))
182			if i == m.cursor {
183				line = selectedStyle.Render("в–ё " + strings.TrimLeft(line, " "))
184			}
185			b.WriteString(line + "\n")
186		}
187		return b.String()
188	}
189	
190	func (m model) viewOptions() string {
191		var b strings.Builder
192		b.WriteString("Options for: " + m.sel.Session.DisplayLabel() + "\n\n")
193		toggles := []struct {
194			label string
195			on    bool
196		}{
197			{"Include subagents", m.sel.IncludeSubagents},
198			{"Redact secrets", m.sel.Redact},
199			{"Open in browser when done", m.sel.Open},
200		}
201		for i, t := range toggles {
202			check := "[ ]"
203			if t.on {
204				check = "[x]"
205			}
206			line := fmt.Sprintf("%s %s", check, t.label)
207			if m.optCursor == i {
208				line = optionStyle.Render("в–ё " + line)
209			} else {
210				line = "  " + line
211			}
212			b.WriteString(line + "\n")
213		}
214		gen := "Generate report"
215		if m.optCursor == 3 {
216			gen = optionStyle.Render("в–ё " + gen)
217		} else {
218			gen = "  " + gen
219		}
220		b.WriteString("\n" + gen + "\n\n")
221		b.WriteString(mutedStyle.Render("space toggle В· enter confirm В· esc back В· q quit") + "\n")
222		return b.String()
223	}
224	
225	// Run launches the browser and returns the user's selection.
226	func Run(groups []discovery.ProjectGroup) (Selection, error) {
227		if len(groups) == 0 {
228			return Selection{Canceled: true}, fmt.Errorf("no sessions found under ~/.claude/projects")
229		}
230		m := newModel(groups)
231		p := tea.NewProgram(m)
232		res, err := p.Run()
233		if err != nil {
234			return Selection{}, err
235		}
236		fm := res.(model)
237		return fm.sel, nil
238	}

Read~/IdeaProjects/cc-what-have-i-done/internal/discovery/discovery.go
{
  "file_path": "~/IdeaProjects/cc-what-have-i-done/internal/discovery/discovery.go"
}
1	// Package discovery finds Claude Code session transcripts under
2	// ~/.claude/projects and builds a lightweight index for listing and selection.
3	package discovery
4	
5	import (
6		"bufio"
7		"encoding/json"
8		"fmt"
9		"os"
10		"path/filepath"
11		"sort"
12		"strings"
13		"time"
14	)
15	
16	// SessionInfo is a lightweight index entry for one transcript file. It is built
17	// by a cheap scan and does not parse the full timeline.
18	type SessionInfo struct {
19		ID           string
20		FilePath     string
21		ProjectDir   string // encoded directory name
22		ProjectPath  string // decoded absolute path
23		Title        string
24		FirstPrompt  string
25		ModTime      time.Time
26		MessageCount int
27		HasSubagents bool
28	}
29	
30	// ProjectGroup groups a project's sessions.
31	type ProjectGroup struct {
32		ProjectDir  string
33		ProjectPath string
34		Sessions    []SessionInfo
35	}
36	
37	// EncodeProjectDir maps an absolute cwd to its ~/.claude/projects dir name.
38	func EncodeProjectDir(cwd string) string {
39		return strings.ReplaceAll(cwd, "/", "-")
40	}
41	
42	// DecodeProjectDir maps a projects dir name back to an absolute path.
43	//
44	// This is best-effort and lossy: the encoding used for ~/.claude/projects
45	// directory names replaces every "/" with "-", so a decode cannot distinguish
46	// an original path separator from a literal "-" inside a path segment (e.g.
47	// "cc-what-have-i-done" decodes to "cc/what/have/i/done"). Callers that need
48	// the true path should prefer the "cwd" field recorded in transcript records
49	// and only fall back to this function when no such record is available.
50	func DecodeProjectDir(name string) string {
51		return strings.ReplaceAll(name, "-", "/")
52	}
53	
54	// DefaultRoot returns ~/.claude/projects.
55	func DefaultRoot() (string, error) {
56		home, err := os.UserHomeDir()
57		if err != nil {
58			return "", err
59		}
60		return filepath.Join(home, ".claude", "projects"), nil
61	}
62	
63	// scanLine is the subset of fields needed to index a session cheaply.
64	type scanLine struct {
65		Type        string          `json:"type"`
66		AiTitle     string          `json:"aiTitle"`
67		IsSidechain bool            `json:"isSidechain"`
68		Timestamp   string          `json:"timestamp"`
69		Cwd         string          `json:"cwd"`
70		Message     json.RawMessage `json:"message"`
71	}
72	
73	// indexFile reads a jsonl file and produces a SessionInfo without a full parse.
74	func indexFile(path, projectDir string) (SessionInfo, error) {
75		f, err := os.Open(path)
76		if err != nil {
77			return SessionInfo{}, err
78		}
79		defer f.Close()
80	
81		fi, err := f.Stat()
82		if err != nil {
83			return SessionInfo{}, err
84		}
85	
86		info := SessionInfo{
87			ID:          strings.TrimSuffix(filepath.Base(path), ".jsonl"),
88			FilePath:    path,
89			ProjectDir:  projectDir,
90			ProjectPath: DecodeProjectDir(projectDir),
91			ModTime:     fi.ModTime(),
92		}
93	
94		sc := bufio.NewScanner(f)
95		sc.Buffer(make([]byte, 0, 1024*1024), 16*1024*1024)
96		cwdSet := false
97		for sc.Scan() {
98			var l scanLine
99			if err := json.Unmarshal(sc.Bytes(), &l); err != nil {
100				continue // tolerate malformed lines
101			}
102			switch l.Type {
103			case "ai-title":
104				if l.AiTitle != "" {
105					info.Title = l.AiTitle
106				}
107			case "user", "assistant":
108				info.MessageCount++
109				if l.IsSidechain {
110					info.HasSubagents = true
111				}
112				if l.Type == "user" && info.FirstPrompt == "" {
113					info.FirstPrompt = firstPromptText(l.Message)
114				}
115				if !cwdSet && l.Cwd != "" {
116					info.ProjectPath = l.Cwd
117					cwdSet = true
118				}
119			}
120		}
121		if info.Title == "" {
122			info.Title = truncate(info.FirstPrompt, 60)
123		}
124		return info, nil
125	}
126	
127	// firstPromptText extracts a plain-text preview from a user message whose
128	// content is either a JSON string or an array of blocks.
129	func firstPromptText(raw json.RawMessage) string {
130		if len(raw) == 0 {
131			return ""
132		}
133		var msg struct {
134			Content json.RawMessage `json:"content"`
135		}
136		if err := json.Unmarshal(raw, &msg); err != nil {
137			return ""
138		}
139		var s string
140		if json.Unmarshal(msg.Content, &s) == nil {
141			return strings.TrimSpace(s)
142		}
143		var blocks []struct {
144			Type string `json:"type"`
145			Text string `json:"text"`
146		}
147		if json.Unmarshal(msg.Content, &blocks) == nil {
148			for _, b := range blocks {
149				if b.Type == "text" {
150					return strings.TrimSpace(b.Text)
151				}
152			}
153		}
154		return ""
155	}
156	
157	func truncate(s string, n int) string {
158		s = strings.TrimSpace(s)
159		r := []rune(s)
160		if len(r) <= n {
161			return s
162		}
163		return string(r[:n-1]) + "вЂ¦"
164	}
165	
166	// Scan indexes every session under root (the projects directory), grouped by
167	// project. Groups are ordered by most-recent session first; sessions within a
168	// group are newest-first.
169	func Scan(root string) ([]ProjectGroup, error) {
170		entries, err := os.ReadDir(root)
171		if err != nil {
172			return nil, err
173		}
174		var groups []ProjectGroup
175		for _, e := range entries {
176			if !e.IsDir() {
177				continue
178			}
179			dir := filepath.Join(root, e.Name())
180			files, err := filepath.Glob(filepath.Join(dir, "*.jsonl"))
181			if err != nil {
182				return nil, err
183			}
184			var sessions []SessionInfo
185			for _, fp := range files {
186				si, err := indexFile(fp, e.Name())
187				if err != nil {
188					continue
189				}
190				sessions = append(sessions, si)
191			}
192			if len(sessions) == 0 {
193				continue
194			}
195			sort.Slice(sessions, func(i, j int) bool {
196				return sessions[i].ModTime.After(sessions[j].ModTime)
197			})
198			groups = append(groups, ProjectGroup{
199				ProjectDir:  e.Name(),
200				ProjectPath: sessions[0].ProjectPath,
201				Sessions:    sessions,
202			})
203		}
204		sort.Slice(groups, func(i, j int) bool {
205			return groups[i].Sessions[0].ModTime.After(groups[j].Sessions[0].ModTime)
206		})
207		return groups, nil
208	}
209	
210	// DisplayLabel returns a human-friendly one-line label for a session.
211	func (s SessionInfo) DisplayLabel() string {
212		if s.Title != "" {
213			return s.Title
214		}
215		if s.FirstPrompt != "" {
216			return s.FirstPrompt
217		}
218		return s.ID
219	}
220	
221	// FindSession resolves a session id or unambiguous prefix across all projects.
222	func FindSession(root, idOrPrefix string) (SessionInfo, error) {
223		groups, err := Scan(root)
224		if err != nil {
225			return SessionInfo{}, err
226		}
227		var matches []SessionInfo
228		for _, g := range groups {
229			for _, s := range g.Sessions {
230				if s.ID == idOrPrefix {
231					return s, nil // exact wins immediately
232				}
233				if strings.HasPrefix(s.ID, idOrPrefix) {
234					matches = append(matches, s)
235				}
236			}
237		}
238		switch len(matches) {
239		case 0:
240			return SessionInfo{}, fmt.Errorf("no session matching %q", idOrPrefix)
241		case 1:
242			return matches[0], nil
243		default:
244			return SessionInfo{}, fmt.Errorf("ambiguous prefix %q matches %d sessions", idOrPrefix, len(matches))
245		}
246	}

{
  "file_path": "~/IdeaProjects/cc-what-have-i-done/cmd/ccwhid/run.go"
}
1	package main
2	
3	import (
4		"fmt"
5		"os"
6		"os/exec"
7		"path/filepath"
8		"runtime"
9		"strings"
10	
11		"github.com/saigyo/cc-what-have-i-done/internal/discovery"
12		"github.com/saigyo/cc-what-have-i-done/internal/redact"
13		"github.com/saigyo/cc-what-have-i-done/internal/render"
14		"github.com/saigyo/cc-what-have-i-done/internal/transcript"
15	)
16	
17	func resolveOutDir(opts *options, si discovery.SessionInfo) string {
18		if opts.out != "" {
19			return opts.out
20		}
21		short := si.ID
22		if len(short) > 8 {
23			short = short[:8]
24		}
25		return filepath.Join("ccwhid-report", short)
26	}
27	
28	// resolveSession picks a session from flags. It returns needTUI=true when the
29	// user gave no selector.
30	func resolveSession(opts *options, root string) (discovery.SessionInfo, bool, error) {
31		switch {
32		case opts.session != "":
33			si, err := discovery.FindSession(root, opts.session)
34			return si, false, err
35		case opts.latest:
36			return latestSession(opts, root)
37		default:
38			return discovery.SessionInfo{}, true, nil
39		}
40	}
41	
42	func latestSession(opts *options, root string) (discovery.SessionInfo, bool, error) {
43		groups, err := discovery.Scan(root)
44		if err != nil {
45			return discovery.SessionInfo{}, false, err
46		}
47		for _, g := range groups {
48			if opts.project != "" && !matchProject(g, opts.project) {
49				continue
50			}
51			if len(g.Sessions) > 0 {
52				return g.Sessions[0], false, nil
53			}
54		}
55		return discovery.SessionInfo{}, false, fmt.Errorf("no sessions found")
56	}
57	
58	func matchProject(g discovery.ProjectGroup, want string) bool {
59		return g.ProjectPath == want ||
60			strings.EqualFold(filepath.Base(g.ProjectPath), want) ||
61			strings.Contains(g.ProjectPath, want)
62	}
63	
64	// generate parses, redacts, and renders a session, returning the output dir.
65	func generate(opts *options, si discovery.SessionInfo) (string, error) {
66		outDir := resolveOutDir(opts, si)
67		if err := ensureOutDir(outDir, opts.force); err != nil {
68			return "", err
69		}
70		sess, err := transcript.ParseFile(si.FilePath, transcript.Options{
71			IncludeSubagents: opts.includeSubagents,
72		})
73		if err != nil {
74			return "", err
75		}
76		if si.ID != "" {
77			sess.ID = si.ID
78		}
79		if sess.SkippedLines > 0 {
80			fmt.Fprintf(os.Stderr, "warning: skipped %d malformed line(s)\n", sess.SkippedLines)
81		}
82		if !opts.noRedact {
83			home, _ := os.UserHomeDir()
84			redact.Session(&sess, home)
85		}
86		if err := render.Site(sess, outDir, render.Options{Title: opts.title}); err != nil {
87			return "", err
88		}
89		return outDir, nil
90	}
91	
92	func ensureOutDir(dir string, force bool) error {
93		entries, err := os.ReadDir(dir)
94		if err != nil {
95			if os.IsNotExist(err) {
96				return os.MkdirAll(dir, 0o755)
97			}
98			return err
99		}
100		if len(entries) > 0 && !force {
101			return fmt.Errorf("output directory %q is not empty (use --force to overwrite)", dir)
102		}
103		return nil
104	}
105	
106	// openInBrowser opens path (a file or dir) in the default browser.
107	func openInBrowser(path string) error {
108		index := filepath.Join(path, "index.html")
109		abs, err := filepath.Abs(index)
110		if err != nil {
111			return err
112		}
113		url := "file://" + abs
114		switch runtime.GOOS {
115		case "darwin":
116			return exec.Command("open", url).Start()
117		case "windows":
118			return exec.Command("rundll32", "url.dll,FileProtocolHandler", url).Start()
119		default:
120			return exec.Command("xdg-open", url).Start()
121		}
122	}
